2x" data-file-width="177" data-file-height="174" /></th></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Orkney</b> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="/\xc9\x94\xcb\x90r/: &#39;ar&#39; in &#39;war&#39;">\xc9\x94\xcb\x90r</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span></span>/</a></span></span> (<a href="/wiki/Scots_language" title="Scots language">Scots</a>: <i lang="sco">Orkney</i>), also known as the <b>Orkney Islands</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;Notes 1&#93;</a></sup> is an <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Isles" title="Northern Isles">Northern Isles</a> of <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, situated off the north coast of Great Britain. Orkney is 16 kilometres (10&#160;mi) north of the coast of <a href="/wiki/Caithness" title="Caithness">Caithness</a> and comprises approximately 70 islands, of which 20 are inhabited.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NRS_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRS-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\nThe largest island, <a href="/wiki/Mainland,_Orkney" title="Mainland, Orkney">Mainland</a>, is often referred to as "the Mainland". It has an area of 523 square kilometres (202&#160;sq&#160;mi), making it the <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_Scotland" title="List of islands of Scotland">sixth-largest Scottish island</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_the_British_Isles" title="List of islands of the British Isles">tenth-largest island in the British Isles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The largest settlement and administrative centre is <a href="/wiki/Kirkwall" title="Kirkwall">Kirkwall</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A form of the name dates to the pre-Roman era and the islands have been inhabited for at least 8,500 years, originally occupied by <a href="/wiki/Mesolithic" title="Mesolithic">Mesolithic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> tribes and then by the <a href="/wiki/Picts" title="Picts">Picts</a>.  Orkney contains some of the oldest and best-preserved Neolithic sites in Europe, and the "<a href="/wiki/Heart_of_Neolithic_Orkney" title="Heart of Neolithic Orkney">Heart of Neolithic Orkney</a>" is a designated <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>.\n</p><p>Orkney was invaded and forcibly <a href="/wiki/Annexation" title="Annexation">annexed</a> by <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Norway" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Norway">Norway</a> in 875 and settled by the <a href="/wiki/Norsemen" title="Norsemen">Norse</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Scotland" title="Parliament of Scotland">Scottish Parliament</a> then re-annexed the <a href="/wiki/Earldom_of_Orkney" title="Earldom of Orkney">earldom</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Scotland" title="Kingdom of Scotland">Scottish Crown</a> in 1472, following the failed payment of a <a href="/wiki/Dowry" title="Dowry">dowry</a> for <a href="/wiki/James_III_of_Scotland" title="James III of Scotland">James III</a>\'s bride <a href="/wiki/Margaret_of_Denmark,_Queen_of_Scotland" title="Margaret of Denmark, Queen of Scotland">Margaret of Denmark</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> \nOrkney is one of the 32 <a href="/wiki/Subdivisions_of_Scotland" title="Subdivisions of Scotland">council areas</a> of Scotland, a <a href="/wiki/Orkney_(Scottish_Parliament_constituency)" title="Orkney (Scottish Parliament constituency)">constituency</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament" title="Scottish Parliament">Scottish Parliament</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Lieutenancy_areas_of_Scotland" title="Lieutenancy areas of Scotland">lieutenancy area</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Counties of Scotland">historic county</a>. The local council is <a href="/wiki/Orkney_Islands_Council" title="Orkney Islands Council">Orkney Islands Council</a>, one of only three Councils in Scotland with a majority of elected members who are <a href="/wiki/Independent_politician" title="Independent politician">independents</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;Notes 2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In addition to the Mainland, most of the islands are in two groups, the North and South Isles, all of which have an underlying geological base of <a href="/wiki/Old_Red_Sandstone" title="Old Red Sandstone">Old Red Sandstone</a>. The climate is mild and the soils are extremely fertile, most of the land being farmed. Agriculture is the most important sector of the economy. The significant wind and marine energy resources are of growing importance, and the island generates more than its total yearly electricity demand using renewables. The local people are known as Orcadians and have a distinctive <a href="/wiki/Orcadian_dialect" title="Orcadian dialect">dialect</a> of <a href="/wiki/Insular_Scots" title="Insular Scots">Insular Scots</a> and a rich inheritance of folklore. There is an abundance of marine and avian wildlife.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24"><a href="#Festivals"><span class="tocnumber">9.4</span> <span class="toctext">Festivals</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#Language,_literature_and_folklore"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Language, literature and folklore</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#Footnotes"><span class="tocnumber">14.1</span> <span class="toctext">Footnotes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31"><a href="#Citations"><span class="tocnumber">14.2</span> references</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Blaeu_-_Atlas_of_Scotland_1654_-_ORCADVM_ET_SCHETLANDI%C3%86_-_Orkney_and_Shetland.jpg" class="image"><img alt="An old map of two island groups with the &quot;Orcades&quot; at left and &quot;Schetlandia&quot; at right. A coat of arms at top left shows a red lion rampant on a yellow shield flanked by two white unicorns. A second heraldic device is shown at bottom right below the &quot;Oceanus Germanicus&quot;. This has two mermaids surrounding a tabula containing very small writing, topped by a yellow and blue shield." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Blaeu_-_Atlas_of_Scotland_1654_-_ORCADVM_ET_SCHETLANDI%C3%86_-_Orkney_and_Shetland.jpg/220px-Blaeu_-_Atlas_of_Scotland_1654_-_ORCADVM_ET_SCHETLANDI%C3%86_-_Orkney_and_Shetland.jpg" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Blaeu_-_Atlas_of_Scotland_1654_-_ORCADVM_ET_SCHETLANDI%C3%86_-_Orkney_and_Shetland.jpg/330px-Blaeu_-_Atlas_of_Scotland_1654_-_ORCADVM_ET_SCHETLANDI%C3%86_-_Orkney_and_Shetland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Blaeu_-_Atlas_of_Scotland_1654_-_ORCADVM_ET_SCHETLANDI%C3%86_-_Orkney_and_Shetland.jpg/440px-Blaeu_-_Atlas_of_Scotland_1654_-_ORCADVM_ET_SCHETLANDI%C3%86_-_Orkney_and_Shetland.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6300" data-file-height="4800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Blaeu_-_Atlas_of_Scotland_1654_-_ORCADVM_ET_SCHETLANDI%C3%86_-_Orkney_and_Shetland.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Willem_Blaeu" title="Willem Blaeu">Blaeu\'s</a> 1654 map of Orkney and Shetland. Map makers at this time continued to use the original Latin name "Orcades" .</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Pytheas" title="Pytheas">Pytheas</a> of <a href="/wiki/Marseille" title="Marseille">Massilia</a> visited Britain \xe2\x80\x93 probably sometime between 322 and 285&#160;BCE \xe2\x80\x93 and described it as triangular in shape, with a northern tip called <i>Orcas</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Breeze_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Breeze-13">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\nThis may have referred to <a href="/wiki/Dunnet_Head" title="Dunnet Head">Dunnet Head</a>, from which Orkney is visible.<sup id="cite_ref-jarehro_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jarehro-14">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Writing in the 1st century&#160;AD, the Roman geographer <a href="/wiki/Pomponius_Mela" title="Pomponius Mela">Pomponius Mela</a> called the islands <i><i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Orcades</i></i>, as did <a href="/wiki/Tacitus" title="Tacitus">Tacitus</a> in 98 AD, claiming that his father-in-law <a href="/wiki/Gnaeus_Julius_Agricola" title="Gnaeus Julius Agricola">Agricola</a> had "discovered and subjugated the Orcades hitherto unknown"<sup id="cite_ref-jarehro_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jarehro-14">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> (although both Mela and <a href="/wiki/Pliny_the_Elder" title="Pliny the Elder">Pliny</a> had previously referred to the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-Breeze_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Breeze-13">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>)\nEtymologists usually interpret the element <i><i lang="xpi" title="Pictish language text">orc-</i></i> as a <a href="/wiki/Picts" title="Picts">Pictish</a> tribal name meaning "young pig" or "young <a href="/wiki/Wild_boar" title="Wild boar">boar</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;Notes 3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Waugh_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Waugh-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Speakers of <a href="/wiki/Old_Irish" title="Old Irish">Old Irish</a> referred to the islands as <i><i lang="sga" title="Old Irish language text">Insi Orc</i></i> "island of the pigs".<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-jaroo_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jaroo-19">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> is known as <i><i lang="cy" title="Welsh language text">Ynysoedd Erch</i></i> in modern <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a> and <i><i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">Arcaibh</i></i> in modern <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Scottish Gaelic</a>, the <i><i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">-aibh</i></i> representing a <a href="/wiki/Fossilization_(linguistics)" title="Fossilization (linguistics)">fossilized</a> <a href="/wiki/Prepositional_case" title="Prepositional case">prepositional case</a> ending.\n</p><p>The Anglo-Saxon monk <a href="/wiki/Bede" title="Bede">Bede</a> refers to the islands as <i><i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Orcades insulae</i></i> in his seminal work <i><a href="/wiki/Ecclesiastical_History_of_the_English_People" title="Ecclesiastical History of the English People">Ecclesiastical History of the English People</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Norwegians" title="Norwegians">Norwegian</a> settlers arriving from the late ninth century reinterpreted <i>orc</i> as the <a href="/wiki/Old_Norse" title="Old Norse">Old Norse</a> <i><i lang="non" title="Old Norse language text">orkn</i></i> "<a href="/wiki/Pinniped" title="Pinniped">seal</a>" and added <i><i lang="non" title="Old Norse language text"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ey#Old_Norse" class="extiw" title="wikt:ey">eyjar</a></i></i> "islands" to the end<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> so the name became <i><i lang="non" title="Old Norse language text">Orkneyjar</i></i> "Seal Islands". The plural suffix <i><i lang="non" title="Old Norse language text">-jar</i></i> was later removed in English leaving the modern name "Orkney". According to the <i><a href="/wiki/Historia_Norwegi%C3%A6" title="Historia Norwegi\xc3\xa6">Historia Norwegi\xc3\xa6</a></i>, Orkney was named after an <a href="/wiki/Earl" title="Earl">earl</a> called Orkan.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Norse knew <a href="/wiki/Mainland,_Orkney" title="Mainland, Orkney">Mainland Orkney</a> as <i><i lang="non" title="Old Norse language text">Megenland</i></i> "Mainland" or as <i><i lang="non" title="Old Norse language text">Hrossey</i></i> "Horse Island".<sup id="cite_ref-Haswell-Smith_2004_p._354_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haswell-Smith_2004_p._354-23">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The island is sometimes referred to as <i>Pomona</i> (or <i>Pomonia</i>), a name that stems from a sixteenth-century mistranslation by <a href="/wiki/George_Buchanan" title="George Buchanan">George Buchanan</a>, which has rarely been used locally.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Orkney" title="History of Orkney">History of Orkney</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RingofBrodgarJM.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Four large standing stones sit in a field of grass and heather. They are illuminated by reddish sunlight and they cast long shadows to the left. A lake and low hills lie beyond." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/RingofBrodgarJM.jpg/170px-RingofBrodgarJM.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/RingofBrodgarJM.jpg/255px-RingofBrodgarJM.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/RingofBrodgarJM.jpg/340px-RingofBrodgarJM.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RingofBrodgarJM.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ring_of_Brodgar" title="Ring of Brodgar">Ring of Brodgar</a>, on the island of <a href="/wiki/Mainland,_Orkney" title="Mainland, Orkney">Mainland, Orkney</a></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Prehistory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_Orkney" title="Prehistoric Orkney">Prehistoric Orkney</a></div>\n<p>A charred <a href="/wiki/Hazelnut" title="Hazelnut">hazelnut</a> shell, recovered in 2007 during excavations in Tankerness on the Mainland has been dated to 6820\xe2\x80\x936660 BC indicating the presence of Mesolithic nomadic tribes.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The earliest known permanent settlement is at <a href="/wiki/Knap_of_Howar" title="Knap of Howar">Knap of Howar</a>, a Neolithic farmstead on the island of <a href="/wiki/Papa_Westray" title="Papa Westray">Papa Westray</a>, which dates from 3500 BC. The village of <a href="/wiki/Skara_Brae" title="Skara Brae">Skara Brae</a>, Europe\'s best-preserved Neolithic settlement, is believed to have been inhabited from around 3100 BC.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Other remains from that era include the <a href="/wiki/Standing_Stones_of_Stenness" title="Standing Stones of Stenness">Standing Stones of Stenness</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Maeshowe" title="Maeshowe">Maeshowe</a> <a href="/wiki/Passage_grave" title="Passage grave">passage grave</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ring_of_Brodgar" title="Ring of Brodgar">Ring of Brodgar</a> and other standing stones. Many of the Neolithic settlements were abandoned around 2500 BC, possibly due to changes in the climate.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> fewer large stone structures were built although the great ceremonial circles continued in use<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> as metalworking was slowly introduced to Britain from Europe over a lengthy period.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> There are relatively few Orcadian sites dating from this era although there is the impressive <a href="/w/index.php?title=Plumcake_Mound&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Plumcake Mound (page does not exist)">Plumcake Mound</a> near the Ring of Brodgar and various islands sites such as Tofts Ness on <a href="/wiki/Sanday,_Orkney" title="Sanday, Orkney">Sanday</a> and the remains of two houses on <a href="/wiki/Holm_of_Faray" title="Holm of Faray">Holm of Faray</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Iron_Age">Iron Age</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Iron Age">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Midhowe_Broch.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A semi-circular stone wall at left hints at the existence of a large and ancient building and to the right are the ruins of various other stone structures. In the background a low cliff divides a body of water from grassy fields." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Midhowe_Broch.jpg/220px-Midhowe_Broch.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Midhowe_Broch.jpg/330px-Midhowe_Broch.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Midhowe_Broch.jpg/440px-Midhowe_Broch.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Midhowe_Broch.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Midhowe_Broch" title="Midhowe Broch">Midhowe Broch</a> on the west coast of <a href="/wiki/Rousay" title="Rousay">Rousay</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Excavations at Quanterness on the Mainland have revealed an <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_roundhouse" title="Atlantic roundhouse">Atlantic roundhouse</a> built about 700 BC and similar finds have been made at Bu on the Mainland and Pierowall Quarry on Westray.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The most impressive <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> structures of Orkney are the ruins of later round towers called "<a href="/wiki/Broch" title="Broch">brochs</a>" and their associated settlements such as the <a href="/wiki/Broch_of_Burroughston" class="mw-redirect" title="Broch of Burroughston">Broch of Burroughston</a><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Broch_of_Gurness" title="Broch of Gurness">Broch of Gurness</a>. The nature and origin of these buildings is a subject of ongoing debate. Other structures from this period include <a href="/wiki/Souterrain" title="Souterrain">underground storehouses</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wheelhouse_(archaeology)" title="Wheelhouse (archaeology)">aisled roundhouses</a>, the latter usually in association with earlier broch sites.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Roman</a> invasion of Britain the "King of Orkney" was one of 11 British leaders who is said to have submitted to the Emperor <a href="/wiki/Claudius" title="Claudius">Claudius</a> in AD 43 at <a href="/wiki/Camulodunum" title="Camulodunum">Colchester</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;Notes 4&#93;</a></sup> After the Agricolan fleet had come and gone, possibly anchoring at <a href="/wiki/Shapinsay" title="Shapinsay">Shapinsay</a>, direct Roman influence seems to have been limited to trade rather than conquest.<sup id="cite_ref-Thomson4_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thomson4-44">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By the late Iron Age, Orkney was part of the <a href="/wiki/Picts" title="Picts">Pictish</a> kingdom, and although the <a href="/wiki/Archaeological" class="mw-redirect" title="Archaeological">archaeological</a> remains from this period are less impressive there is every reason to suppose the fertile soils and rich seas of Orkney provided the Picts with a comfortable living.<sup id="cite_ref-Thomson4_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thomson4-44">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;Notes 5&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A1l_Riata" title="D\xc3\xa1l Riata">Dalriadic</a> <a href="/wiki/Gaels" title="Gaels">Gaels</a> began to influence the islands towards the close of the Pictish era, perhaps principally through the role of <a href="/wiki/Celtic_Christianity" title="Celtic Christianity">Celtic</a> <a href="/wiki/Missionary" title="Missionary">missionaries</a>, as evidenced by several islands bearing the epithet "Papa" in commemoration of these preachers.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> However, before the Gaelic presence could establish itself the Picts were gradually dispossessed by the <a href="/wiki/North_Germanic_peoples" title="North Germanic peoples">Norse</a> from the late 8th century onwards. The nature of this transition is controversial, and theories range from peaceful integration to <a href="/wiki/Enslavement" class="mw-redirect" title="Enslavement">enslavement</a> and <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> It has been suggested that an assault by forces from <a href="/wiki/Fortriu" title="Fortriu">Fortriu</a> in 681 in which Orkney was "annihilated" may have led to a weakening of the local power base and helped the Norse come to prominence.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Norwegian_rule">Norwegian rule</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Norwegian rule">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flateyjarbok_Haraldr_Halfdan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A page from an illuminated manuscript shows two male figures. On the left a seated man wears a red crown and on the right a standing man has long fair hair. Their right hands are clasped together." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flateyjarbok_Haraldr_Halfdan.jpg/220px-Flateyjarbok_Haraldr_Halfdan.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flateyjarbok_Haraldr_Halfdan.jpg/330px-Flateyjarbok_Haraldr_Halfdan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flateyjarbok_Haraldr_Halfdan.jpg/440px-Flateyjarbok_Haraldr_Halfdan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="558" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flateyjarbok_Haraldr_Halfdan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>According to the <i><a href="/wiki/Orkneyinga_saga" title="Orkneyinga saga">Orkneyinga Saga</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Harald_I_of_Norway" class="mw-redirect" title="Harald I of Norway">Harald Fairhair</a> (on the left) took control of Orkney in 875.</div></div></div>\n<p>Both Orkney and <a href="/wiki/Shetland" title="Shetland">Shetland</a> saw a significant influx of Norwegian settlers during the late 8th and early 9th centuries. <a href="/wiki/Viking" class="mw-redirect" title="Viking">Vikings</a> made the islands the headquarters of their <a href="/wiki/Pirate" class="mw-redirect" title="Pirate">pirate</a> expeditions carried out against Norway and the coasts of mainland Scotland. In response, Norwegian king <a href="/wiki/Harald_I_of_Norway" class="mw-redirect" title="Harald I of Norway">Harald Fairhair</a> (Harald H\xc3\xa5rfagre) annexed the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Isles" title="Northern Isles">Northern Isles</a>, comprising Orkney and Shetland, in 875. (It is clear that this story, which appears in the <i>Orkneyinga Saga</i>, is based on the later voyages of <a href="/wiki/Magnus_III_of_Norway" class="mw-redirect" title="Magnus III of Norway">Magnus Barelegs</a> and some scholars believe it to be apocryphal.)<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rognvald_Eysteinsson" title="Rognvald Eysteinsson">Rognvald Eysteinsson</a> received Orkney and Shetland from Harald as an earldom as reparation for the death of his son in battle in Scotland, and then passed the earldom on to his brother <a href="/wiki/Sigurd_Eysteinsson" title="Sigurd Eysteinsson">Sigurd the Mighty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>However, Sigurd\'s line barely survived him and it was <a href="/wiki/Torf-Einarr" title="Torf-Einarr">Torf-Einarr</a>, Rognvald\'s son by a slave, who founded a dynasty that controlled the islands for centuries after his death.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;Notes 6&#93;</a></sup> He was succeeded by his son <a href="/wiki/Thorfinn_Turf-Einarsson,_Earl_of_Orkney" class="mw-redirect" title="Thorfinn Turf-Einarsson, Earl of Orkney">Thorfinn Skull-splitter</a> and during this time the deposed Norwegian King <a href="/wiki/Eric_Bloodaxe" title="Eric Bloodaxe">Eric Bloodaxe</a> often used Orkney as a raiding base before being killed in 954. Thorfinn\'s death and presumed burial at the broch of Hoxa, on <a href="/wiki/South_Ronaldsay" title="South Ronaldsay">South Ronaldsay</a>, led to a long period of dynastic strife.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Peter_nicolai_arbo,_olaf_tryggvasson_king.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A group of warriors in medieval garb surround two men whose postures suggest they are about to embrace. The man on the right is taller, has long fair hair and wears a bright red tunic. The man on the left his balding with short grey hair and a white beard. He wears a long brown cloak." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Peter_nicolai_arbo%2C_olaf_tryggvasson_king.jpg/220px-Peter_nicolai_arbo%2C_olaf_tryggvasson_king.jpg" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Peter_nicolai_arbo%2C_olaf_tryggvasson_king.jpg/330px-Peter_nicolai_arbo%2C_olaf_tryggvasson_king.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Peter_nicolai_arbo%2C_olaf_tryggvasson_king.jpg/440px-Peter_nicolai_arbo%2C_olaf_tryggvasson_king.jpg 2x" data-file-width="460" data-file-height="294" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Peter_nicolai_arbo,_olaf_tryggvasson_king.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Artist\'s conception of <a href="/wiki/Olaf_I_of_Norway" class="mw-redirect" title="Olaf I of Norway">King Olaf Tryggvason</a> of Norway, who forcibly Christianised Orkney.<sup id="cite_ref-T69_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-T69-57">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Painting by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Nicolai_Arbo" title="Peter Nicolai Arbo">Peter Nicolai Arbo</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Initially a pagan culture, detailed information about the turn to the Christian religion to the islands of Scotland during the Norse-era is elusive.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The  <i>Orkneyinga Saga</i> suggests the islands were Christianised by <a href="/wiki/Olaf_I_of_Norway" class="mw-redirect" title="Olaf I of Norway">Olaf Tryggvasson</a> in 995 when he stopped at <a href="/wiki/South_Walls" title="South Walls">South Walls</a> on his way from Ireland to Norway. The King summoned the <i><a href="/wiki/Earl" title="Earl">jarl</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Sigurd_the_Stout" title="Sigurd the Stout">Sigurd the Stout</a><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;Notes 7&#93;</a></sup> and said, "I order you and all your subjects to be baptised. If you refuse, I\'ll have you killed on the spot and I swear I will ravage every island with fire and steel." Unsurprisingly, Sigurd agreed and the islands became Christian at a stroke,<sup id="cite_ref-T69_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-T69-57">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> receiving their own <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Orkney" title="Bishop of Orkney">bishop</a> in the early 11th century.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;Notes 8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;Notes 9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Thorfinn_Sigurdsson" class="mw-redirect" title="Thorfinn Sigurdsson">Thorfinn the Mighty</a> was a son of Sigurd and a grandson of <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_II_of_Scotland" title="Malcolm II of Scotland">King M\xc3\xa1el Coluim mac Cin\xc3\xa1eda</a> (Malcolm II of Scotland). Along with Sigurd\'s other sons he ruled Orkney during the first half of the 11th century and extended his authority over a small maritime empire stretching from <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a> to <a href="/wiki/Shetland" title="Shetland">Shetland</a>. Thorfinn died around 1065 and his sons <a href="/wiki/Paul_and_Erlend_Thorfinnsson" title="Paul and Erlend Thorfinnsson">Paul and Erlend</a> succeeded him, fighting at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Stamford_Bridge" title="Battle of Stamford Bridge">Battle of Stamford Bridge</a> in 1066.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Paul and Erlend quarreled as adults and this dispute carried on to the next generation. The <a href="/wiki/Martyr" title="Martyr">martyrdom</a> of <a href="/wiki/Magnus_Erlendsson,_Earl_of_Orkney" title="Magnus Erlendsson, Earl of Orkney">Magnus Erlendsson</a>, who was killed in April 1116 by his cousin <a href="/wiki/Haakon_Paulsson" title="Haakon Paulsson">Haakon Paulsson</a>, resulted in the building of <a href="/wiki/St._Magnus_Cathedral" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Magnus Cathedral">St. Magnus Cathedral</a>, still today a dominating feature of Kirkwall.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;Notes 10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;Notes 11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kirkwall_cathedral.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A large church made from red and yellow stone with a square tower and a spire on the tower." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Kirkwall_cathedral.jpg/220px-Kirkwall_cathedral.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Kirkwall_cathedral.jpg/330px-Kirkwall_cathedral.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Kirkwall_cathedral.jpg/440px-Kirkwall_cathedral.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kirkwall_cathedral.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/St._Magnus_Cathedral" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Magnus Cathedral">St Magnus Cathedral</a> in Kirkwall</div></div></div>\n<p>Unusually, from c. 1100 onwards the Norse <i>jarls</i> owed allegiance both to Norway for Orkney and to the Scottish crown through their holdings as <a href="/wiki/Earls_of_Caithness" class="mw-redirect" title="Earls of Caithness">Earls of Caithness</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> In 1231 the line of Norse earls, unbroken since Rognvald, ended with <a href="/wiki/Jon_Haraldsson" title="Jon Haraldsson">Jon Haraldsson</a>\'s murder in <a href="/wiki/Thurso" title="Thurso">Thurso</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Earldom_of_Caithness" class="mw-redirect" title="Earldom of Caithness">Earldom of Caithness</a> was granted to <a href="/wiki/Magnus_II,_Earl_of_Orkney" title="Magnus II, Earl of Orkney">Magnus</a>, second son of the <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Angus" title="Earl of Angus">Earl of Angus</a>, whom <a href="/wiki/Haakon_IV_of_Norway" title="Haakon IV of Norway">Haakon IV of Norway</a> confirmed as Earl of Orkney in 1236.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> In 1290, the death of the child princess <a href="/wiki/Margaret,_Maid_of_Norway" title="Margaret, Maid of Norway">Margaret, Maid of Norway</a> in Orkney, en route to mainland Scotland, created a disputed succession that led to the <a href="/wiki/Wars_of_Scottish_Independence" title="Wars of Scottish Independence">Wars of Scottish Independence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-T146_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-T146-74">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;Notes 12&#93;</a></sup> In 1379 the earldom passed to the <a href="/wiki/Clan_Sinclair" title="Clan Sinclair">Sinclair</a> family, who were also barons of <a href="/wiki/Roslin_Castle" title="Roslin Castle">Roslin</a> near <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;Notes 13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Evidence of the Viking presence is widespread, and includes the settlement at the <a href="/wiki/Brough_of_Birsay" title="Brough of Birsay">Brough of Birsay</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> the vast majority of <a href="/wiki/Toponymy" title="Toponymy">place names</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Runic_alphabet" class="mw-redirect" title="Runic alphabet">runic</a> inscriptions at Maeshowe.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;Notes 14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Annexation_by_Scotland">Annexation by Scotland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Annexation by Scotland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:James_III_and_Margaret_of_Denmark.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A picture on a page in an old book. A man at left wears tights and a tunic with a lion rampant design and holds a sword and scepter. A woman at right wears a dress with an heraldic design bordered with ermine and carries a thistle in one hand and a scepter in the other. They stand on a green surface over a legend in Scots that begins &quot;James the Thrid of Nobil Memorie...&quot; (sic) and notes that he &quot;marrit the King of Denmark&#39;s dochter.&quot;" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/James_III_and_Margaret_of_Denmark.jpg/200px-James_III_and_Margaret_of_Denmark.jpg" width="200" height="260" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/James_III_and_Margaret_of_Denmark.jpg/300px-James_III_and_Margaret_of_Denmark.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2a/James_III_and_Margaret_of_Denmark.jpg 2x" data-file-width="346" data-file-height="450" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:James_III_and_Margaret_of_Denmark.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/James_III_of_Scotland" title="James III of Scotland">James III</a> and <a href="/wiki/Margaret_of_Denmark,_Queen_of_Scotland" title="Margaret of Denmark, Queen of Scotland">Margaret</a>, whose betrothal led to Orkney passing from Norway to Scotland.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1468 Orkney was <a href="/wiki/Pledge_(law)" title="Pledge (law)">pledged</a> by <a href="/wiki/Christian_I_of_Denmark" title="Christian I of Denmark">Christian I</a>, in his capacity as King of Norway, as security against the payment of the <a href="/wiki/Dowry" title="Dowry">dowry</a> of his daughter <a href="/wiki/Margaret_of_Denmark,_Queen_of_Scotland" title="Margaret of Denmark, Queen of Scotland">Margaret</a>, betrothed to <a href="/wiki/James_III_of_Scotland" title="James III of Scotland">James III of Scotland</a>. However the money was never paid, and Orkney was annexed by the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Scotland" title="Kingdom of Scotland">Kingdom of Scotland</a> in 1472. <sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;Notes 15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The history of Orkney prior to this time is largely the history of the ruling aristocracy. From now on the ordinary people emerge with greater clarity. An influx of Scottish entrepreneurs helped to create a diverse and independent community that included farmers, fishermen and merchants that called themselves <i>comunitas Orcadie</i> and who proved themselves increasingly able to defend their rights against their feudal overlords.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>From at least the 16th century, boats from mainland Scotland and the Netherlands dominated the local <a href="/wiki/Herring" title="Herring">herring</a> fishery. There is little evidence of an Orcadian fleet until the 19th century but it grew rapidly and 700 boats were involved by the 1840s with Stronsay and later <a href="/wiki/Stromness" title="Stromness">Stromness</a> becoming leading centres of development. <a href="/wiki/Whitefish_(fisheries_term)" title="Whitefish (fisheries term)">White fish</a> never became as dominant as in other Scottish ports.<sup id="cite_ref-Coull_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Coull-89">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 17th century, Orcadians formed the overwhelming majority of employees of the <a href="/wiki/Hudson%27s_Bay_Company" title="Hudson&#39;s Bay Company">Hudson\'s Bay Company</a> in Canada. The harsh climate of Orkney and the Orcadian reputation for sobriety and their boat handling skills made them ideal candidates for the rigours of the Canadian north.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> During this period, burning <a href="/wiki/Kelp" title="Kelp">kelp</a> briefly became a mainstay of the islands\' economy. For example on Shapinsay over 3,000 <a href="/wiki/Long_ton" title="Long ton">long tons</a> (3,048&#160;<a href="/wiki/Tonne" title="Tonne">t</a>) of burned seaweed were produced per annum to make <a href="/wiki/Soda_ash" class="mw-redirect" title="Soda ash">soda ash</a>, bringing in \xc2\xa320,000 to the local economy.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> The industry collapsed suddenly in 1830 after the removal of tariffs on imported <a href="/wiki/Alkali" title="Alkali">alkali</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Agricultural improvements beginning in the 17th century resulted in the enclosure of the commons and ultimately in the Victoria era the emergence of large and well-managed farms using a five-shift rotation system and producing high-quality beef cattle.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the 18th century <a href="/wiki/Jacobite_risings" title="Jacobite risings">Jacobite risings</a>, Orkney was largely Jacobite in its sympathies. At the end of the 1715 rebellion, a large number of Jacobites who had fled north from mainland Scotland sought refuge on Orkney and were helped on to safety in Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> In 1745, the Jacobite lairds on the islands ensured that Orkney remained pro-Jacobite in outlook, and was a safe place to land supplies from Spain to aid their cause. Orkney was the last place in the British Isles that held out for the Jacobites and was not retaken by the <a href="/wiki/Broad_Bottom_Ministry" class="mw-redirect" title="Broad Bottom Ministry">British Government</a> until 24 May 1746, over a month after the defeat of the main Jacobite army at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Culloden" title="Battle of Culloden">Culloden</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_altar_art_of_the_Italian_chapel_of_Orkney_-_geograph.org.uk_-_739607.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/The_altar_art_of_the_Italian_chapel_of_Orkney_-_geograph.org.uk_-_739607.jpg/220px-The_altar_art_of_the_Italian_chapel_of_Orkney_-_geograph.org.uk_-_739607.jpg" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/The_altar_art_of_the_Italian_chapel_of_Orkney_-_geograph.org.uk_-_739607.jpg/330px-The_altar_art_of_the_Italian_chapel_of_Orkney_-_geograph.org.uk_-_739607.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/The_altar_art_of_the_Italian_chapel_of_Orkney_-_geograph.org.uk_-_739607.jpg/440px-The_altar_art_of_the_Italian_chapel_of_Orkney_-_geograph.org.uk_-_739607.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="422" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_altar_art_of_the_Italian_chapel_of_Orkney_-_geograph.org.uk_-_739607.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Italian_Chapel" title="Italian Chapel">Italian Chapel</a> on <a href="/wiki/Lamb_Holm" title="Lamb Holm">Lamb Holm</a> was built and decorated by Italian prisoners of war working on the <a href="/wiki/Churchill_Barriers" title="Churchill Barriers">Churchill Barriers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thom434_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thom434-96">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Orkney was the site of a <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> base at <a href="/wiki/Scapa_Flow" title="Scapa Flow">Scapa Flow</a>, which played a major role in World War I and <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">II</a>. After the <a href="/wiki/Armistice" title="Armistice">Armistice</a> in 1918, the <a href="/wiki/German_High_Seas_Fleet" class="mw-redirect" title="German High Seas Fleet">German High Seas Fleet</a> was transferred in its entirety to Scapa Flow to await a decision on its future. The German sailors opened the sea-cocks and scuttled all the ships. Most ships were salvaged, but the remaining wrecks are now a favoured haunt of recreational divers. One month into World War II, a German <a href="/wiki/U-boat" title="U-boat">U-boat</a> sank the Royal Navy battleship <a href="/wiki/HMS_Royal_Oak_(08)" title="HMS Royal Oak (08)">HMS&#160;<i>Royal Oak</i></a> in Scapa Flow. As a result, <a href="/wiki/Churchill_Barriers" title="Churchill Barriers">barriers</a> were built to close most of the access channels; these had the additional advantage of creating causeways enabling travellers to go from island to island by road instead of being obliged to rely on ferries. The causeways were constructed by Italian prisoners of war, who also constructed the ornate <a href="/wiki/Italian_Chapel" title="Italian Chapel">Italian Chapel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thom434_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thom434-96">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The navy base became run down after the war, eventually closing in 1957. The problem of a declining population was significant in the post-war years, though in the last decades of the 20th century there was a recovery and life in Orkney focused on growing prosperity and the emergence of a relatively classless society.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Orkney was rated as the best place to live in Scotland in both 2013 and 2014 according to the Halifax Quality of Life survey.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview_of_population_trends">Overview of population trends</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Overview of population trends">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the modern era, population peaked in the mid 19th century at just over 32,000 and declined for a century thereafter to a low of fewer than 18,000 in the 1970s. Declines were particularly significant in the outlying islands, some of which remain vulnerable to ongoing losses. Although Orkney is in many ways very distinct from the other islands and archipelagos of Scotland these trends are very similar to those experienced elsewhere.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vis_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vis-100">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> The archipelago\'s population grew by 11% in the decade to 2011 as recorded by the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_2011" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Census 2011">census</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NRS_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRS-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GRO_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GRO-101">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> During the same period <a href="/wiki/List_of_Scottish_islands" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Scottish islands">Scottish island</a> populations as a whole grew by 4% to 103,702.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div>\n\n&#32;\n<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:auto;"><tbody><tr>\n<td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">\n<table class="toccolours" style="width:15em;border-spacing: 0;float:none;clear:none;margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 1em;">\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Orkney_Map.png" class="image"><img alt="A map of the Orkney archipelago showing main transport routes. A small island with a high elevation is at south west. At centre is the largest island, which also has low hills. Ferry routes spread out from there to the smaller islands in the north." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Orkney_Map.png/220px-Orkney_Map.png" width="220" height="261" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Orkney_Map.png/330px-Orkney_Map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Orkney_Map.png/440px-Orkney_Map.png 2x" data-file-width="788" data-file-height="934" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Orkney_Map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Orkney showing main transport routes</div></div></div>\n<p>Orkney is separated from the mainland of Scotland by the <a href="/wiki/Pentland_Firth" title="Pentland Firth">Pentland Firth</a>, a 10-kilometre (6.2&#160;mi) wide seaway between Brough Ness on the island of <a href="/wiki/South_Ronaldsay" title="South Ronaldsay">South Ronaldsay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Duncansby_Head" title="Duncansby Head">Duncansby Head</a> in <a href="/wiki/Caithness" title="Caithness">Caithness</a>. Orkney lies between 58\xc2\xb041\xe2\x80\xb2 and 59\xc2\xb024\xe2\x80\xb2 North, and 2\xc2\xb022\xe2\x80\xb2 and 3\xc2\xb026\xe2\x80\xb2 West, measuring 80 kilometres (50&#160;mi) from northeast to southwest and 47 kilometres (29&#160;mi) from east to west, and covers 975 square kilometres (376&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-OS_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OS-103">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Orkneys are separated from the <a href="/wiki/Shetland_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Shetland Islands">Shetland Islands</a>, a group further out, by a body of water called the <a href="/wiki/Fair_Isle_Channel" title="Fair Isle Channel">Fair Isle Channel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TrevesPineschi1997_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TrevesPineschi1997-105">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The islands are mainly low-lying except for some sharply rising sandstone hills on <a href="/wiki/Hoy" title="Hoy">Hoy</a>, Mainland and Rousay and rugged cliffs on some western coasts. Nearly all of the islands have <a href="/wiki/Loch" title="Loch">lochs</a>, but the watercourses are merely streams draining the high land. The coastlines are indented, and the islands themselves are divided from each other by straits generally called "sounds" or "firths".<sup id="cite_ref-OS_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OS-103">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Brown_2003_p._19_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brown_2003_p._19-106">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Tide" title="Tide">tidal currents</a>, or "roosts" as some of them are called locally,<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> off many of the isles are swift, with frequent whirlpools.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;Notes 16&#93;</a></sup> The islands are notable for the absence of trees, which is partly accounted for by the amount of wind.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Genetic studies have shown that 25% of the gene pool of Orkney derives from Norwegian ancestors who invaded the islands in the 9th century.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Islands">Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Orkney_islands" title="List of Orkney islands">List of Orkney islands</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Mainland">The Mainland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: The Mainland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mainland,_Orkney" title="Mainland, Orkney">Mainland, Orkney</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stromness_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Stone houses crowd around a shore, the gable ends facing the water, with green hills beyond." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Stromness_2.jpg/220px-Stromness_2.jpg" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Stromness_2.jpg/330px-Stromness_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Stromness_2.jpg/440px-Stromness_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="777" data-file-height="562" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stromness_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Stromness" title="Stromness">Stromness</a> on the Mainland is the second largest settlement on Orkney.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Mainland is the largest island of Orkney. Both of Orkney\'s <a href="/wiki/Burgh" title="Burgh">burghs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kirkwall" title="Kirkwall">Kirkwall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stromness" title="Stromness">Stromness</a>, are on this island, which is also the heart of Orkney\'s transportation system, with <a href="/wiki/Ferry" title="Ferry">ferry</a> and air connections to the other islands and to the outside world. The island is more densely populated (75% of Orkney\'s population) than the other islands and has much fertile <a href="/wiki/Farmland_(farming)" class="mw-redirect" title="Farmland (farming)">farmland</a>. The Mainland is split into areas called East and West Mainland. These areas are determined by whether they lie East or West of Kirkwall. The bulk of the mainland lies West of Kirkwall, with comparatively little land lying East of Kirkwall.\nWest Mainland parishes are:\nStromness, Sandwick, Birsay, Harray, Stenness, Orphir, Evie, Rendall and Firth.\nEast Mainland Parishes are:\nSt Ola, Tankerness, St Andrews, Holm and Deerness.\n</p><p>The island is mostly low-lying (especially East Mainland) but with coastal cliffs to the north and west and two sizeable lochs: the <a href="/wiki/Loch_of_Harray" title="Loch of Harray">Loch of Harray</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Loch_of_Stenness" title="Loch of Stenness">Loch of Stenness</a>. The Mainland contains the remnants of numerous <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Picts" title="Picts">Pictish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Viking" class="mw-redirect" title="Viking">Viking</a> constructions. Four of the main Neolithic sites are included in the <a href="/wiki/Heart_of_Neolithic_Orkney" title="Heart of Neolithic Orkney">Heart of Neolithic Orkney</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>, inscribed in 1999.\n</p><p>The other islands in the group are classified as north or south of the Mainland. Exceptions are the remote islets of <a href="/wiki/Sule_Skerry" title="Sule Skerry">Sule Skerry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sule_Stack" title="Sule Stack">Sule Stack</a>, which lie 60 kilometres (37&#160;mi) west of the archipelago, but form part of Orkney for local government purposes. In island names, the <a href="/wiki/Suffix" title="Suffix">suffix</a> "a" or "ay" represents the Norse <i>ey</i>, meaning "island". Those described as "<a href="/wiki/Holm_(island)" title="Holm (island)">holms</a>" are very small.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_North_Isles">The North Isles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: The North Isles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NR_sheep.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/NR_sheep.jpg/220px-NR_sheep.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/NR_sheep.jpg/330px-NR_sheep.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/NR_sheep.jpg/440px-NR_sheep.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NR_sheep.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/North_Ronaldsay_(sheep)" class="mw-redirect" title="North Ronaldsay (sheep)">North Ronaldsay sheep</a> are a <a href="/wiki/Feral" title="Feral">semi-feral</a> breed that has evolved to eat seaweed.<sup id="cite_ref-SheepCentre_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SheepCentre-112">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Their unique genetic inheritance makes them of interest to conservationists.<sup id="cite_ref-Lawson_et_al._2007._113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson_et_al._2007.-113">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>The northern group of islands is the most extensive and consists of a large number of moderately sized islands, linked to the Mainland by ferries and by air services. Farming, fishing and tourism are the main sources of income for most of the islands.\n</p><p>The most northerly is <a href="/wiki/North_Ronaldsay" title="North Ronaldsay">North Ronaldsay</a>, which lies 4 kilometres (2&#160;mi) beyond its nearest neighbour, <a href="/wiki/Sanday,_Orkney" title="Sanday, Orkney">Sanday</a>. To the west is <a href="/wiki/Westray" title="Westray">Westray</a>, which has a population of 550. It is connected by ferry and air to <a href="/wiki/Papa_Westray" title="Papa Westray">Papa Westray</a>, also known as "Papay". <a href="/wiki/Eday" title="Eday">Eday</a> is at the centre of the <a href="/wiki/North_Isles" title="North Isles">North Isles</a>. The centre of the island is <a href="/wiki/Moorland" title="Moorland">moorland</a> and the island\'s main industries have been peat extraction and <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a> <a href="/wiki/Quarry" title="Quarry">quarrying</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Rousay" title="Rousay">Rousay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egilsay" title="Egilsay">Egilsay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gairsay" title="Gairsay">Gairsay</a> lie north of the west Mainland across the <a href="/wiki/Eynhallow_Sound" title="Eynhallow Sound">Eynhallow Sound</a>. Rousay is well known for its ancient monuments, including the Quoyness <a href="/wiki/Chambered_cairn" title="Chambered cairn">chambered cairn</a> and Egilsay has the ruins of the only round-towered church in Orkney. <a href="/wiki/Wyre,_Orkney" title="Wyre, Orkney">Wyre</a> to the south-east contains the site of Cubbie Roo\'s castle. <a href="/wiki/Stronsay" title="Stronsay">Stronsay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Papa_Stronsay" title="Papa Stronsay">Papa Stronsay</a> lie much further to the east across the Stronsay Firth. <a href="/wiki/Auskerry" title="Auskerry">Auskerry</a> is south of Stronsay and has a population of only five. <a href="/wiki/Shapinsay" title="Shapinsay">Shapinsay</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Balfour_Castle" title="Balfour Castle">Balfour Castle</a> are a short distance north of Kirkwall.\n</p><p>Other small uninhabited islands in the North Isles group include: <a href="/wiki/Calf_of_Eday" title="Calf of Eday">Calf of Eday</a>, <a href="/wiki/Damsay" title="Damsay">Damsay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eynhallow" title="Eynhallow">Eynhallow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Faray" title="Faray">Faray</a>, <a href="/wiki/Helliar_Holm" title="Helliar Holm">Helliar Holm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Holm_of_Faray" title="Holm of Faray">Holm of Faray</a>, <a href="/wiki/Holm_of_Huip" title="Holm of Huip">Holm of Huip</a>, <a href="/wiki/Holm_of_Papa" title="Holm of Papa">Holm of Papa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Holm_of_Scockness" title="Holm of Scockness">Holm of Scockness</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kili_Holm" title="Kili Holm">Kili Holm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Linga_Holm" class="mw-redirect" title="Linga Holm">Linga Holm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muckle_Green_Holm" title="Muckle Green Holm">Muckle Green Holm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rusk_Holm" title="Rusk Holm">Rusk Holm</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sweyn_Holm" title="Sweyn Holm">Sweyn Holm</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hoy_Lighthouse_RLH.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A tall white lighthouse with a brown stripe around the parapet and dark coloured lantern sits on a rocky shore. A white wall obscures the lower floor of grey stone buildings gathered around its base." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Hoy_Lighthouse_RLH.jpg/170px-Hoy_Lighthouse_RLH.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Hoy_Lighthouse_RLH.jpg/255px-Hoy_Lighthouse_RLH.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Hoy_Lighthouse_RLH.jpg/340px-Hoy_Lighthouse_RLH.jpg 2x" data-file-width="575" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hoy_Lighthouse_RLH.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Hoy_Lighthouse" class="mw-redirect" title="Hoy Lighthouse">Hoy Lighthouse</a> on <a href="/wiki/Graemsay" title="Graemsay">Graemsay</a></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_South_Isles">The South Isles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: The South Isles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The southern group of islands surrounds <a href="/wiki/Scapa_Flow" title="Scapa Flow">Scapa Flow</a>. <a href="/wiki/Hoy" title="Hoy">Hoy</a> is the second largest of the Orkney Isles and <a href="/wiki/Ward_Hill,_Hoy" title="Ward Hill, Hoy">Ward Hill</a> at its northern end is the highest elevation in the archipelago. The <a href="/wiki/Old_Man_of_Hoy" title="Old Man of Hoy">Old Man of Hoy</a> is a well-known <a href="/wiki/Stack_(geology)" title="Stack (geology)">seastack</a>. <a href="/wiki/Burray" title="Burray">Burray</a> lies to the east of Scapa Flow and is linked by causeway to South Ronaldsay, which hosts the cultural events, the Festival of the Horse and the Boys\' <a href="/wiki/Ploughing_Match" class="mw-redirect" title="Ploughing Match">Ploughing Match</a> on the third Saturday in August.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> It is also the location of the Neolithic <a href="/wiki/Tomb_of_the_Eagles" title="Tomb of the Eagles">Tomb of the Eagles</a>. <a href="/wiki/Graemsay" title="Graemsay">Graemsay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flotta" title="Flotta">Flotta</a> are both linked by ferry to the Mainland and Hoy, and the latter is known for its large oil terminal. <a href="/wiki/South_Walls" title="South Walls">South Walls</a> has a 19th-century <a href="/wiki/Martello_tower" title="Martello tower">Martello tower</a> and is connected to Hoy by the Ayre. South Ronaldsay, Burray, <a href="/wiki/Glims_Holm" title="Glims Holm">Glims Holm</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lamb_Holm" title="Lamb Holm">Lamb Holm</a> are connected by road to the Mainland by the <a href="/wiki/Churchill_Barriers" title="Churchill Barriers">Churchill Barriers</a>.\n</p><p>Uninhabited South Islands include: <a href="/wiki/Calf_of_Flotta" title="Calf of Flotta">Calf of Flotta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cava_(island)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cava (island)">Cava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copinsay" title="Copinsay">Copinsay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corn_Holm" title="Corn Holm">Corn Holm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fara,_Orkney" title="Fara, Orkney">Fara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glims_Holm" title="Glims Holm">Glims Holm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hunda" title="Hunda">Hunda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lamb_Holm" title="Lamb Holm">Lamb Holm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rysa_Little" title="Rysa Little">Rysa Little</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switha" title="Switha">Switha</a> and <a href="/wiki/Swona" title="Swona">Swona</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Pentland_Skerries" title="Pentland Skerries">Pentland Skerries</a> lie further south, closer to the Scottish mainland.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Orkney" title="Geology of Orkney">Geology of Orkney</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:OldManofHoycloseJM.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A tall perpendicular stack of brown rock stands in the sunlight in front of a shore with high cliffs that lie in the shadows." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/OldManofHoycloseJM.jpg/170px-OldManofHoycloseJM.jpg" width="170" height="242" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/OldManofHoycloseJM.jpg/255px-OldManofHoycloseJM.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/OldManofHoycloseJM.jpg/340px-OldManofHoycloseJM.jpg 2x" data-file-width="533" data-file-height="759" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:OldManofHoycloseJM.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Old_Man_of_Hoy" title="Old Man of Hoy">Old Man of Hoy</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The superficial rock of Orkney is almost entirely <a href="/wiki/Old_Red_Sandstone" title="Old Red Sandstone">Old Red Sandstone</a>, mostly of Middle <a href="/wiki/Devonian" title="Devonian">Devonian</a> age.<sup id="cite_ref-Millennium_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Millennium-115">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> As in the neighbouring mainland county of <a href="/wiki/Caithness" title="Caithness">Caithness</a>, this sandstone rests upon the <a href="/wiki/Metamorphic_rock" title="Metamorphic rock">metamorphic</a> rocks of the <a href="/wiki/Moine_Supergroup" title="Moine Supergroup">Moine</a> series, as may be seen on the Mainland, where a narrow strip is exposed between Stromness and Inganess, and again in the small island of <a href="/wiki/Graemsay" title="Graemsay">Graemsay</a>; they are represented by grey <a href="/wiki/Gneiss" title="Gneiss">gneiss</a> and <a href="/wiki/Granite" title="Granite">granite</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:OrkneyGeologyMap.png" class="image"><img alt="A map of the geology of Orkney. Hoy to the south-west is predominantly formed from Hoy/Eday Sandstones. The Mainland at centre is largely Stromness flagstones with Rousay flagstones to the east. The North and South Isles are a mixture of Eday and Rousay sandstones." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/OrkneyGeologyMap.png/220px-OrkneyGeologyMap.png" width="220" height="261" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/OrkneyGeologyMap.png/330px-OrkneyGeologyMap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/OrkneyGeologyMap.png/440px-OrkneyGeologyMap.png 2x" data-file-width="709" data-file-height="840" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:OrkneyGeologyMap.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Geology of Orkney</div></div></div>\n<p>The Middle Devonian is divided into three main groups. The lower part of the sequence, mostly <a href="/wiki/Eifelian" title="Eifelian">Eifelian</a> in age, is dominated by lacustrine beds of the lower and upper Stromness Flagstones that were deposited in <a href="/wiki/Orcadian_Basin" title="Orcadian Basin">Lake Orcadie</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> The later Rousay flagstone formation is found throughout much of the North and South Isles and East Mainland.<sup id="cite_ref-Brown_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brown-118">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Old Man of Hoy is formed from sandstone of the uppermost Eday group that is up to 800 metres (870&#160;yd) thick in places. It lies unconformably upon steeply inclined flagstones, the interpretation of which is a matter of continuing debate.<sup id="cite_ref-Brown_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brown-118">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Devonian and older rocks of Orkney are cut by a series of WSW-ENE to N-S trending faults, many of which were active during deposition of the Devonian sequences.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>  A strong <a href="/wiki/Syncline" title="Syncline">synclinal</a> fold traverses Eday and Shapinsay, the axis trending north-south.\n</p><p>Middle Devonian <a href="/wiki/Basalt" title="Basalt">basaltic</a> <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_rock" title="Volcanic rock">volcanic rocks</a> are found on western Hoy, on Deerness in eastern Mainland and on Shapinsay. Correlation between the Hoy volcanics and the other two exposures has been proposed, but differences in chemistry means this remains uncertain.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lamprophyre" title="Lamprophyre">Lamprophyre</a> <a href="/wiki/Dike_(geology)" title="Dike (geology)">dykes</a> of Late <a href="/wiki/Permian" title="Permian">Permian</a> age are found throughout Orkney.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Glacial_striation" title="Glacial striation">Glacial striation</a> and the presence of <a href="/wiki/Chalk" title="Chalk">chalk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flint" title="Flint">flint</a> <a href="/wiki/Glacial_erratic" title="Glacial erratic">erratics</a> that originated from the bed of the North Sea demonstrate the influence of ice action on the <a href="/wiki/Geomorphology" title="Geomorphology">geomorphology</a> of the islands. Boulder <a href="/wiki/Clay" title="Clay">clay</a> is also abundant and <a href="/wiki/Moraine" title="Moraine">moraines</a> cover substantial areas.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Orkney has a cool temperate climate that is remarkably mild and steady for such a northerly <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">latitude</a>, due to the influence of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">Gulf Stream</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> The average temperature for the year is 8&#160;\xc2\xb0C (46&#160;\xc2\xb0F); for winter 4&#160;\xc2\xb0C (39&#160;\xc2\xb0F) and for summer 12&#160;\xc2\xb0C (54&#160;\xc2\xb0F).<sup id="cite_ref-met_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-met-125">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The average annual rainfall varies from 850 millimetres (33&#160;in) to 940 millimetres (37&#160;in).<sup id="cite_ref-met_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-met-125">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Winds are a key feature of the climate and even in summer there are almost constant breezes. In winter, there are frequent strong winds, with an average of 52 hours of gales being recorded annually.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>To tourists, one of the fascinations of the islands is their "nightless" summers. On the <a href="/wiki/Midsummer" title="Midsummer">longest day</a>, the sun rises at 04:00 and sets at 22:29 <a href="/wiki/British_Summer_Time" title="British Summer Time">BST</a>  and complete darkness is unknown. This long twilight is known in the Northern Isles as the "simmer dim".<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Winter nights are long. On the <a href="/wiki/Shortest_day" class="mw-redirect" title="Shortest day">shortest day</a> the sun rises at 09:05 and sets at 15:16.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> At this time of year the <a href="/wiki/Aurora_borealis" class="mw-redirect" title="Aurora borealis">aurora borealis</a> can occasionally be seen on the northern horizon during moderate auroral activity.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The averages table below is for largest settlement Kirkwall\'s weather station.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable collapsible" style="width:90%;
