color:#FFFFFF;">32.2\n</td>\n<td style="background: #767676; color:#FFFFFF;">59.3\n</td>\n<td style="background: #ACAC9B; color:#000000;">98.2\n</td>\n<td style="background: #C0C025; color:#000000;">136.8\n</td>\n<td style="background: #D5D500; color:#000000;">190.0\n</td>\n<td style="background: #C5C503; color:#000000;">148.6\n</td>\n<td style="background: #BBBB3E; color:#000000;">132.2\n</td>\n<td style="background: #BABA45; color:#000000;">129.7\n</td>\n<td style="background: #B1B17E; color:#000000;">105.3\n</td>\n<td style="background: #8A8A8A; color:#FFFFFF;">75.8\n</td>\n<td style="background: #4B4B4B; color:#FFFFFF;">40.1\n</td>\n<td style="background: #2C2C2C; color:#FFFFFF;">24.5\n</td>\n<td style="background: #ACAC98; color:#000000; border-left-width:medium">1,172.4\n</td></tr>\n\n\n<tr>\n<td colspan="14" style="text-align:center;font-size:95%;">Source &#35;1: Met Office<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="14" style="text-align:center; font-size:95%;">Source &#35;2: Royal Dutch Meteorological Institute/KNMI<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Orkney is represented in the <a href="/wiki/British_House_of_Commons" class="mw-redirect" title="British House of Commons">House of Commons</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/Orkney_and_Shetland_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Orkney and Shetland (UK Parliament constituency)">Orkney and Shetland</a> <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_constituencies" title="United Kingdom constituencies">constituency</a>, which elects one <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of Parliament">Member of Parliament</a> (MP), the current incumbent being <a href="/wiki/Alistair_Carmichael" title="Alistair Carmichael">Alistair Carmichael</a>. This seat has been held by the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a> or their predecessors the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_(UK)" title="Liberal Party (UK)">Liberal Party</a> since 1950, longer than any other they represent in Great Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament" title="Scottish Parliament">Scottish Parliament</a> the <a href="/wiki/Orkney_(Scottish_Parliament_constituency)" title="Orkney (Scottish Parliament constituency)">Orkney</a> constituency elects one <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_Scottish_Parliament" title="Member of the Scottish Parliament">Member of the Scottish Parliament</a> (MSP) by the <a href="/wiki/Plurality_voting_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Plurality voting system">first past the post</a> system. The current MSP is <a href="/wiki/Liam_McArthur" title="Liam McArthur">Liam McArthur</a> of the Liberal Democrats.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> Before McArthur the MSP was <a href="/wiki/Jim_Wallace,_Baron_Wallace_of_Tankerness" title="Jim Wallace, Baron Wallace of Tankerness">Jim Wallace</a>, who was previously <a href="/wiki/Deputy_First_Minister_of_Scotland" title="Deputy First Minister of Scotland">Deputy First Minister</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> Orkney is within the <a href="/wiki/Highlands_and_Islands_(Scottish_Parliament_region)" class="mw-redirect" title="Highlands and Islands (Scottish Parliament region)">Highlands and Islands</a> <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament_constituencies_and_regions" title="Scottish Parliament constituencies and regions">electoral region</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Orkney_Islands_Council" title="Orkney Islands Council">Orkney Islands Council</a> consists of 21 members, 20 of whom are <a href="/wiki/Independent_politician" title="Independent politician">independent</a>, that is they do not stand as representatives of a political party. The remaining councillor represents the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Green_Party" title="Scottish Green Party">Green Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Orkney Movement, a political party that supported devolution for Orkney from the rest of Scotland, contested the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_1987" title="United Kingdom general election, 1987">1987 general election</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Orkney_and_Shetland_Movement" title="Orkney and Shetland Movement">Orkney and Shetland Movement</a> (a coalition of the Orkney movement and its equivalent for Shetland). The <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">Scottish National Party</a> chose not to contest the seat to give the movement a "free run". Their candidate, John Goodlad, came 4th with 3,095 votes, 14.5% of those cast, but the experiment has not been repeated.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_independence_referendum,_2014" title="Scottish independence referendum, 2014">2014 Scottish independence referendum</a> 67.2% of voters in Orkney voted No to the question "Should Scotland be an independent country?" This was the highest&#160;% No vote in any council area in Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> Turnout for the referendum was at 83.7% in Orkney with 10,004 votes cast in the area against independence by comparison to 4,883 votes for independence.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The soil of Orkney is generally very fertile and most of the land is taken up by farms, agriculture being by far the most important sector of the economy and providing employment for a quarter of the workforce.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> More than 90% of agricultural land is used for grazing for sheep and cattle, with cereal production utilising about 4% (4,200 hectares (10,000 acres)) and woodland occupying only 134 hectares (330 acres).<sup id="cite_ref-OER_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OER-143">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Fishing has declined in importance, but still employed 345 individuals in 2001, about 3.5% of the islands\' economically active population, the modern industry concentrating on herring, white fish, <a href="/wiki/Homarus_gammarus" title="Homarus gammarus">lobsters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crab" title="Crab">crabs</a> and other shellfish, and <a href="/wiki/Salmon" title="Salmon">salmon</a> fish farming.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;Notes 17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Today, the traditional sectors of the economy export <a href="/wiki/Beef" title="Beef">beef</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cheese" title="Cheese">cheese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Whisky" title="Whisky">whisky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beer" title="Beer">beer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">fish</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Seafood" title="Seafood">seafood</a>. In recent years there has been growth in other areas including tourism, food and beverage manufacture, jewellery, knitwear, and other crafts production, construction and oil transportation through the <a href="/wiki/Flotta" title="Flotta">Flotta</a> oil terminal.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Retailing accounts for 17.5% of total employment,<sup id="cite_ref-OER_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OER-143">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> and public services also play a significant role, employing a third of the islands\' workforce.<sup id="cite_ref-HIE_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HIE-146">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2007, of the 1,420 <a href="/wiki/VAT" class="mw-redirect" title="VAT">VAT</a> registered enterprises 55% were in agriculture, forestry and fishing, 12% in manufacturing and construction, 12% in wholesale, retail and repairs, and 5% in hotels and restaurants. A further 5% were public service related.<sup id="cite_ref-OER_143-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OER-143">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> 55% of these businesses employ between 5 and 49 people.<sup id="cite_ref-HIE_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HIE-146">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Power">Power</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Power">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pelamis_at_EMEC.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A long red tube lies in the water under dark, cloud-covered skies with black hills in the distance." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Pelamis_at_EMEC.jpg/220px-Pelamis_at_EMEC.jpg" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Pelamis_at_EMEC.jpg/330px-Pelamis_at_EMEC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Pelamis_at_EMEC.jpg/440px-Pelamis_at_EMEC.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1419" data-file-height="876" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pelamis_at_EMEC.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Pelamis_wave_energy_converter" class="mw-redirect" title="Pelamis wave energy converter">Pelamis</a> on site at <a href="/wiki/European_Marine_Energy_Centre" title="European Marine Energy Centre">EMEC\'s</a> wave testing site off Billia Croo</div></div></div>\n<p>Orkney has significant wind and marine energy resources, and <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_in_Scotland" title="Renewable energy in Scotland">renewable energy</a> has recently come into prominence. Although Orkney is connected to the mainland, it generates over <a href="/wiki/100%25_renewable_energy" title="100% renewable energy">100% of its net power from renewables</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> This comes mainly from wind turbines situated across Orkney.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Marine_Energy_Centre" title="European Marine Energy Centre">European Marine Energy Centre</a> (EMEC) is a research facility operating a grid-connected wave test site at Billia Croo, off the west coast of the Orkney Mainland, and a tidal power test site in the Fall of Warness, off the northern island of Eday.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> At the official opening of the Eday project the site was described as "the first of its kind in the world set up to provide developers of wave and tidal energy devices with a purpose-built performance testing facility."<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;Notes 18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During 2007 <a href="/wiki/Scottish_and_Southern_Energy" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish and Southern Energy">Scottish and Southern Energy</a> plc in conjunction with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Strathclyde" title="University of Strathclyde">University of Strathclyde</a> began the implementation of a Regional Power Zone in the Orkney archipelago. This scheme (that may be the first of its kind in the world) involves "active network management" that will make better use of existing infrastructure and allow a further 15MW of new "non-firm generation" output from renewables onto the network.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Highlands_and_Islands_Airports_Limited" class="mw-redirect" title="Highlands and Islands Airports Limited">Highland and Islands Airports</a> operates the main airport in Orkney, <a href="/wiki/Kirkwall_Airport" title="Kirkwall Airport">Kirkwall Airport</a>. <a href="/wiki/Loganair" title="Loganair">Loganair</a>, provides services to the Scottish mainland (<a href="/wiki/Aberdeen_Airport" title="Aberdeen Airport">Aberdeen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Airport" title="Edinburgh Airport">Edinburgh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Airport" title="Glasgow Airport">Glasgow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Inverness_Airport" title="Inverness Airport">Inverness</a>), as well as to <a href="/wiki/Sumburgh_Airport" title="Sumburgh Airport">Sumburgh Airport</a> in Shetland.<sup id="cite_ref-visork_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-visork-153">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Within Orkney, the council operates airfields on most of the larger islands including <a href="/wiki/Stronsay_Airport" title="Stronsay Airport">Stronsay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eday_Airport" title="Eday Airport">Eday</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Ronaldsay_Airport" title="North Ronaldsay Airport">North Ronaldsay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Westray_Airport" title="Westray Airport">Westray</a>, <a href="/wiki/Papa_Westray_Airport" title="Papa Westray Airport">Papa Westray</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sanday_Airport" title="Sanday Airport">Sanday</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Loganair_Westray_to_Papa_Westray_route" class="mw-redirect" title="Loganair Westray to Papa Westray route">shortest scheduled air service in the world</a>, between the islands of Westray and Papa Westray, is scheduled at two minutes duration<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> but can take less than one minute if the wind is in the right direction.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ferry">Ferry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Ferry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ferry_at_Whale_Geo_pier,_Westray_-_geograph.org.uk_-_33804.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Ferry_at_Whale_Geo_pier%2C_Westray_-_geograph.org.uk_-_33804.jpg/220px-Ferry_at_Whale_Geo_pier%2C_Westray_-_geograph.org.uk_-_33804.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Ferry_at_Whale_Geo_pier%2C_Westray_-_geograph.org.uk_-_33804.jpg/330px-Ferry_at_Whale_Geo_pier%2C_Westray_-_geograph.org.uk_-_33804.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Ferry_at_Whale_Geo_pier%2C_Westray_-_geograph.org.uk_-_33804.jpg/440px-Ferry_at_Whale_Geo_pier%2C_Westray_-_geograph.org.uk_-_33804.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ferry_at_Whale_Geo_pier,_Westray_-_geograph.org.uk_-_33804.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/MV_Earl_Thorfinn" title="MV Earl Thorfinn">MV Earl Thorfinn</a> arrives at <a href="/wiki/Westray" title="Westray">Westray</a>. <a href="/wiki/Orkney_Ferries" title="Orkney Ferries">Orkney Ferries</a> operate a fleet of inter-island ferries.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Ferries serve both to link Orkney to the rest of Scotland, and also to link together the various islands of the Orkney archipelago. Ferry services operate between Orkney and the Scottish mainland and Shetland on the following routes:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Gills Bay to <a href="/wiki/St_Margaret%27s_Hope" title="St Margaret&#39;s Hope">St Margaret\'s Hope</a> (operated by <a href="/wiki/Pentland_Ferries" title="Pentland Ferries">Pentland Ferries</a>)</li>\n<li>John o\' Groats to <a href="/wiki/Burwick,_Orkney" title="Burwick, Orkney">Burwick</a> on South Ronaldsay (seasonal passenger only service, operated by <a href="/w/index.php?title=John_o%27_Groats_Ferries&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="John o&#39; Groats Ferries (page does not exist)">John o\' Groats Ferries</a>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lerwick,_Shetland" class="mw-redirect" title="Lerwick, Shetland">Lerwick</a> to Kirkwall (operated by <a href="/wiki/NorthLink_Ferries" title="NorthLink Ferries">NorthLink Ferries</a>)</li>\n<li>Aberdeen to Kirkwall (operated by NorthLink Ferries)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Scrabster_Harbour" class="mw-redirect" title="Scrabster Harbour">Scrabster Harbour</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thurso" title="Thurso">Thurso</a> to <a href="/wiki/Stromness" title="Stromness">Stromness</a> (operated by NorthLink Ferries)</li></ul>\n<p>Inter-island ferry services connect all the inhabited islands to Orkney Mainland, and are operated by <a href="/wiki/Orkney_Ferries" title="Orkney Ferries">Orkney Ferries</a>, a company owned by Orkney Islands Council.<sup id="cite_ref-visork_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-visork-153">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Orkney is served by a weekly local newspaper, <a href="/wiki/The_Orcadian" title="The Orcadian">The Orcadian</a>.\n</p><p>A local BBC radio station, <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Orkney" title="BBC Radio Orkney">BBC Radio Orkney</a>, the local opt-out of <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Scotland" title="BBC Radio Scotland">BBC Radio Scotland</a>, broadcasts twice daily, with local news and entertainment.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Orkney also had a <a href="/wiki/Commercial_radio" class="mw-redirect" title="Commercial radio">commercial radio</a> station, <a href="/wiki/The_Superstation_Orkney" title="The Superstation Orkney">The Superstation Orkney</a>, which broadcast to Kirkwall and parts of the mainland and also to most of <a href="/wiki/Caithness" title="Caithness">Caithness</a><sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> until its closure in November 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Moray_Firth_Radio" title="Moray Firth Radio">Moray Firth Radio</a> broadcasts throughout Orkney on AM and from an FM transmitter just outside Thurso. The <a href="/wiki/Community_radio" title="Community radio">community radio</a> station Caithness FM also broadcasts to Orkney.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Orkney is home to the Orkney Library and Archive, located in <a href="/wiki/Kirkwall" title="Kirkwall">Kirkwall</a>, Scotland, on the mainland. The Library service provides access to over 145,000 items.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> They have a wide range of fiction and non-fiction titles available for loan as well as audiobooks, maps, eBooks, music CDs, and DVDs.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> Orkney Library and Archive operates a Mobile Library Service that serves the rural parishes and islands of Orkney. The Mobile Library carries a wide range of books and audio books suitable for all ages and is completely free to use.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Orkney Library is also popular on Twitter as the rival of another Scottish library in <a href="/wiki/Shetland" title="Shetland">Shetland</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals">Festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The islands are the home of several international festivals, including the <a href="/wiki/Orkney_International_Science_Festival" title="Orkney International Science Festival">Orkney International Science Festival</a> in September, a folk festival in May, and the <a href="/wiki/St_Magnus_Festival" title="St Magnus Festival">St Magnus International Arts Festival</a> in June.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Language.2C_literature_and_folklore"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Language,_literature_and_folklore">Language, literature and folklore</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Language, literature and folklore">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Odin-Stone_sketch.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="A black and white line drawing of a tall standing stone that is wider at the top than the base. It has a long vertical crack on the right-hand side and there is a small hole that goes right through it near the ground. A lake and hill are in the background." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Odin-Stone_sketch.jpeg/170px-Odin-Stone_sketch.jpeg" width="170" height="232" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Odin-Stone_sketch.jpeg/255px-Odin-Stone_sketch.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8d/Odin-Stone_sketch.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="270" data-file-height="368" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Odin-Stone_sketch.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Odin Stone</div></div></div>\n<p>At the beginning of recorded history, the islands were inhabited by the <a href="/wiki/Picts" title="Picts">Picts</a>, whose language was Brythonic.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;Notes 19&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ogham" title="Ogham">Ogham</a> script on the <a href="/wiki/Buckquoy_spindle-whorl" title="Buckquoy spindle-whorl">Buckquoy spindle-whorl</a> is cited as evidence for the pre-Norse existence of <a href="/wiki/Old_Irish" title="Old Irish">Old Irish</a> in Orkney.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;Notes 20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the Norse occupation, the <a href="/wiki/Toponymy" title="Toponymy">toponymy</a> of Orkney became almost wholly <a href="/wiki/West_Norse" class="mw-redirect" title="West Norse">West Norse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> The Norse language changed into the local <a href="/wiki/Norn_language" title="Norn language">Norn</a>, which lingered until the end of the 18th century, when it finally died out.<sup id="cite_ref-Lamb_2003_p._250_169-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lamb_2003_p._250-169">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Norn was replaced by the <a href="/wiki/Orcadian_dialect" title="Orcadian dialect">Orcadian dialect</a> of <a href="/wiki/Insular_Scots" title="Insular Scots">Insular Scots</a>. This dialect is at a low ebb due to the pervasive influences of television, education, and the large number of incomers. However, attempts are being made by some writers and radio presenters to revitalise its use<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> and the distinctive sing-song <a href="/wiki/Accent_(dialect)" class="mw-redirect" title="Accent (dialect)">accent</a> and many dialect words of Norse origin remain in use.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;Notes 21&#93;</a></sup> The Orcadian word most frequently encountered by visitors is <i>peedie</i>, meaning <i>small</i>, which may be derived from the French <i>petit</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;Notes 22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Orkney has a rich folklore, and many of the former tales concern <a href="/wiki/Trow_(folklore)" title="Trow (folklore)">trows</a>, an Orcadian form of <a href="/wiki/Troll" title="Troll">troll</a> that draws on the islands\' Scandinavian connections.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> Local customs in the past included marriage ceremonies at the Odin Stone that formed part of the Stones of Stenness.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/King_Lot" title="King Lot">King Lot</a> in certain versions of the <a href="/wiki/Arthurian_legend" class="mw-redirect" title="Arthurian legend">Arthurian legend</a> (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Malory" title="Thomas Malory">Malory</a>) is ruler of Orkney. His sons <a href="/wiki/Gawaine" class="mw-redirect" title="Gawaine">Gawaine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agravaine" class="mw-redirect" title="Agravaine">Agravaine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gareth" title="Gareth">Gareth</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gaheris" title="Gaheris">Gaheris</a> are major characters in the <a href="/wiki/Matter_of_Britain" title="Matter of Britain">Matter of Britain</a>.\n</p><p>The best known literary figures from modern Orkney are the poet <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Muir" title="Edwin Muir">Edwin Muir</a>, the poet and novelist <a href="/wiki/George_Mackay_Brown" title="George Mackay Brown">George Mackay Brown</a>, and the novelist <a href="/wiki/Eric_Linklater" title="Eric Linklater">Eric Linklater</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Orcadians">Orcadians</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Orcadians">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Orcadians" title="Orcadians">Orcadians</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Bridge_of_Brodgar,_Stenness,_1875._By_Walter_Hugh_Patton_(1828-1895).tif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/The_Bridge_of_Brodgar%2C_Stenness%2C_1875._By_Walter_Hugh_Patton_%281828-1895%29.tif/lossy-page1-220px-The_Bridge_of_Brodgar%2C_Stenness%2C_1875._By_Walter_Hugh_Patton_%281828-1895%29.tif.jpg" width="220" height="125" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/The_Bridge_of_Brodgar%2C_Stenness%2C_1875._By_Walter_Hugh_Patton_%281828-1895%29.tif/lossy-page1-330px-The_Bridge_of_Brodgar%2C_Stenness%2C_1875._By_Walter_Hugh_Patton_%281828-1895%29.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/The_Bridge_of_Brodgar%2C_Stenness%2C_1875._By_Walter_Hugh_Patton_%281828-1895%29.tif/lossy-page1-440px-The_Bridge_of_Brodgar%2C_Stenness%2C_1875._By_Walter_Hugh_Patton_%281828-1895%29.tif.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2343" data-file-height="1329" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Bridge_of_Brodgar,_Stenness,_1875._By_Walter_Hugh_Patton_(1828-1895).tif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Bridge of Brodgar, Stenness, 1875. By Walter Hugh Patton (1828\xe2\x80\x931895).</div></div></div>\n<p>An <a href="/wiki/Orcadian" class="mw-redirect" title="Orcadian">Orcadian</a> is a native of Orkney, a term that reflects a strongly held identity with a tradition of understatement.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> Although the annexation of the earldom by Scotland took place over five centuries ago in 1472, some Orcadians regard themselves as Orcadians first and <a href="/wiki/Scottish_people" title="Scottish people">Scots</a> second.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> However in response to the national identity question in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_2011" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Census 2011">2011 Scotland Census</a>, self-reported levels of <a href="/wiki/Scottish_national_identity" title="Scottish national identity">Scottish identity</a> in Orkney were in line with the national average.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Scottish mainland is often referred to as "Scotland" in Orkney, with "the mainland" referring to <a href="/wiki/Mainland,_Orkney" title="Mainland, Orkney">Mainland, Orkney</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> The archipelago also has a distinct culture, with traditions of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Highlands" title="Scottish Highlands">Scottish Highlands</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Tartan" title="Tartan">tartan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clans" class="mw-redirect" title="Clans">clans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bagpipes" title="Bagpipes">bagpipes</a> not indigenous to the culture of the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> However, at least two tartans with Orkney connections have been registered and a tartan has been designed for Sanday by one of the island\'s residents,<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> and there are pipe bands in Orkney.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Native Orcadians refer to the non-native residents of the islands as "ferry loupers", ("loup" meaning "jump" in the <a href="/wiki/Scots_language" title="Scots language">Scots language</a> <sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>) a term that has been in use for nearly two centuries at least.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;Notes 23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_history">Natural history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Natural history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Seals_hauled_out_by_Lyrie_Geo,_Hoy,_Orkney_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2472901.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Seals_hauled_out_by_Lyrie_Geo%2C_Hoy%2C_Orkney_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2472901.jpg/170px-Seals_hauled_out_by_Lyrie_Geo%2C_Hoy%2C_Orkney_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2472901.jpg" width="170" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Seals_hauled_out_by_Lyrie_Geo%2C_Hoy%2C_Orkney_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2472901.jpg/255px-Seals_hauled_out_by_Lyrie_Geo%2C_Hoy%2C_Orkney_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2472901.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Seals_hauled_out_by_Lyrie_Geo%2C_Hoy%2C_Orkney_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2472901.jpg/340px-Seals_hauled_out_by_Lyrie_Geo%2C_Hoy%2C_Orkney_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2472901.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1300" data-file-height="1678" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Seals_hauled_out_by_Lyrie_Geo,_Hoy,_Orkney_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2472901.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Seals hauled out at Lyrie Geo on <a href="/wiki/Hoy" title="Hoy">Hoy</a>. Orkney has an abundance of wildlife.</div></div></div>\n<p>Orkney has an abundance of wildlife, especially of <a href="/wiki/Grey_seal" title="Grey seal">grey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harbor_seal" title="Harbor seal">common seals</a> and seabirds such as <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_puffin" title="Atlantic puffin">puffins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kittiwake" title="Kittiwake">kittiwakes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black_guillemot" title="Black guillemot">tysties</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raven" title="Raven">ravens</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Great_skua" title="Great skua">bonxies</a>. Whales, dolphins, and <a href="/wiki/European_otter" class="mw-redirect" title="European otter">otters</a> are also seen around the coasts. Inland the <a href="/wiki/Orkney_vole" title="Orkney vole">Orkney vole</a>, a distinct subspecies of the <a href="/wiki/Common_vole" title="Common vole">common vole</a> introduced by <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> humans, is an <a href="/wiki/Endemic" class="mw-redirect" title="Endemic">endemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SNH_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SNH-194">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> There are five distinct varieties, found on the islands of Sanday, Westray, Rousay, South Ronaldsay, and the Mainland, all the more remarkable as the species is absent on mainland Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The coastline is well known for its colourful flowers including <a href="/wiki/Aster_tripolium" class="mw-redirect" title="Aster tripolium">sea aster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scilla_verna" title="Scilla verna">sea squill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armeria_maritima" title="Armeria maritima">sea thrift</a>, <a href="/wiki/Limonium" title="Limonium">common sea-lavender</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erica_cinerea" title="Erica cinerea">bell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Calluna" title="Calluna">common heather</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Primula_scotica" title="Primula scotica">Scottish primrose</a> is found only on the coasts of Orkney and nearby Caithness and <a href="/wiki/Sutherland" title="Sutherland">Sutherland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Brown_2003_p._19_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brown_2003_p._19-106">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SNH_194-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SNH-194">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> Although stands of trees are generally rare, a small forest named <a href="/wiki/Happy_Valley_(garden)" title="Happy Valley (garden)">Happy Valley</a> with 700 trees and lush gardens was created from a boggy hillside near Stenness during the second half of the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/North_Ronaldsay_sheep" title="North Ronaldsay sheep">North Ronaldsay sheep</a> is an unusual breed of domesticated animal, subsisting largely on a diet of <a href="/wiki/Seaweed" title="Seaweed">seaweed</a>, since they are confined to the foreshore for most of the year to conserve the limited grazing inland.<sup id="cite_ref-SheepCentre2_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SheepCentre2-198">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> The island was also a habitat for the Atlantic <a href="/wiki/Walrus" title="Walrus">walrus</a> until the mid-16th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Roy,1960_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roy,1960-199">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Orkney char (<i><a href="/wiki/Salvelinus_inframundus" title="Salvelinus inframundus">Salvelinus inframundus</a></i>)  used to live in Heldale Water on Hoy. It has been considered <a href="/wiki/Local_extinction" title="Local extinction">locally extinct</a> since 1908.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The introduction of alien <a href="/wiki/Stoats" class="mw-redirect" title="Stoats">stoats</a> just prior to 2015, a natural predator of the common vole and thus of the Orkney vole,<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> may be harming native bird populations.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 27em; -webkit-column-width: 27em; column-width: 27em;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_prehistoric_Scotland" title="Timeline of prehistoric Scotland">Timeline of prehistoric Scotland</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_Scotland" title="Prehistoric Scotland">Prehistoric Scotland</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Florv%C3%A5g" title="Battle of Florv\xc3\xa5g">Battle of Florv\xc3\xa5g</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Orkney" title="Bishop of Orkney">Bishop of Orkney</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Orkney" title="Coat of arms of Orkney">Coat of arms of Orkney</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_places_in_Orkney" title="List of places in Orkney">List of places in Orkney</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Orkney_Club" title="Orkney Club">Orkney Club</a></li>\n<li><a Kolsson</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Udal_Law" class="mw-redirect" title="Udal Law">Udal Law</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Category:Parishes_of_Orkney" title="Category:Parishes of Orkney">Parishes of Orkney</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Constitutional_status_of_Orkney,_Shetland_and_the_Western_Isles" title="Constitutional status of Orkney, Shetland and the Western Isles">Constitutional status of Orkney, Shetland and the Western Isles</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Solar_eclipse_of_1_May_1185" title="Solar eclipse of 1 May 1185">Solar eclipse of 1 May 1185</a></li></ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Footnotes">Footnotes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orkney&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Footnotes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-3">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"The Orkneys" is used by non-Orcadians and does have historical precedent, yet it is clear that this is frowned upon by the residents.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-12">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The other independent-run Councils are <a href="/wiki/Shetland" title="Shetland">Shetland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Comhairle_nan_Eilean_Siar_election,_2007" title="Comhairle nan Eilean Siar election, 2007">Comhairle nan Eilean Siar</a>. <a href="/wiki/Moray" title="Moray">Moray</a> is run by a Conservative/Independent coalition.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The proto-Celtic root <i>&#42;<span lang="cel" title="Proto-Celtic language text">\xcf\x86orko-</span></i>, can mean either pig or <a href="/wiki/Salmon" title="Salmon">salmon</a>, thus giving an alternative of "island(s) of (the) salmon".<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-43"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-43">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Thomson (2008) suggests that there was an element of Roman "boasting" involved, given that it was known to them that the <i>Orcades</i> lay at the northern extremity of the British Isles.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Similarly, Ritchie describes Tacitus\' claims that Rome "conquered" Orkney as "a political puff, for there is no evidence of Roman military presence".<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-46"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-46">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">They were certainly politically organised. Ritchie notes the presence of an Orcadian ruler at the court of a Pictish high king at <a href="/wiki/Inverness" title="Inverness">Inverness</a> in 565 AD.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-54"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-54">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Sigurd The Mighty\'s son Gurthorm ruled for a single winter after Sigurd\'s death and died childless. Rognvald\'s son Hallad inherited the title but, unable to constrain Danish raids on Orkney, he gave up the earldom and returned to Norway, which according to the <i><a href="/wiki/Orkneyinga_saga" title="Orkneyinga saga">Orkneyinga Saga</a></i> "everyone thought was a huge joke."<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-59"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-59">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Sigurd the Stout was Thorfinn Skull-splitter\'s grandson.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-62"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-62">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The first recorded bishop was <a href="/wiki/Henry_of_Lund" title="Henry of Lund">Henry of Lund</a> (also known as "the Fat") who was appointed sometime prior to 1035.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The bishopric appears to have been under the authority of the Archbishops of <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_York" title="Archbishop of York">York</a> and of <a href="/wiki/Archbishopric_of_Bremen" title="Archbishopric of Bremen">Hamburg-Bremen</a> at different times during the early period and from the mid twelfth century to 1472 was subordinate to the <a href="/wiki/Archdiocese_of_Nidaros" class="mw-redirect" title="Archdiocese of Nidaros">Archbishop of Nidaros</a> (today\'s <a href="/wiki/Trondheim" title="Trondheim">Trondheim</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-65"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-65">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">When the sagas were written down Orkney had been Christian for 200 years or more<sup id="cite_ref-Thomson66_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thomson66-63">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> and this conversion tale has been described as "blatantly unhistorical".<sup id="cite_ref-Beuer143_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beuer143-64">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-68"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-68">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Scandinavian peoples, relatively recent converts to Christianity, had a tendency to confer martyrdom and sainthood on leading figures of the day who met violent deaths. Magnus and Haakon Paulsson had been co-rulers of Orkney, and although he had a reputation for piety, there is no suggestion that Magnus died for his Christian faith.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-70"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-70">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"St Magnus Cathedral still dominates the Kirkwall skyline \xe2\x80\x93 a familiar, and comforting sight, to Kirkwallians around the world."<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-75"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-75">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">It is often believed that the princess\'s death is associated with the village of <a href="/wiki/St_Margaret%27s_Hope" title="St Margaret&#39;s Hope">St Margaret\'s Hope</a> on South Ronaldsay but there is no evidence for this other than the coincidence of the name.<sup id="cite_ref-T146_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-T146-74">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-79"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-79">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The notion that <a href="/wiki/Henry_I_Sinclair,_Earl_of_Orkney" title="Henry I Sinclair, Earl of Orkney">Henry</a> the first Sinclair Earl, voyaged to North America many years before <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> has gained some currency of late.<sup id="cite_ref-Haswell-Smith_2004_p._354_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haswell-Smith_2004_p._354-23">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The idea is however dismissed out of hand by many scholars. For example, Thomson (2008) states "Henry\'s fictitious trip to America continues to received a good deal of unfortunate publicity, but it belongs to fantasy rather than real history".<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-83"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-83">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Maeshowe inscriptions date from the 12th century.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-86"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-86">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Apparently without the knowledge of the Norwegian <a href="/wiki/Rigsraadet" class="mw-redirect" title="Rigsraadet">Rigsraadet</a> (Council of the Realm), Christian pawned Orkney for 50,000 Rhenish <a href="/wiki/Guilder" title="Guilder">guilders</a>. On 28 May the next year he also pawned Shetland for 8,000 Rhenish guilders.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> He secured a clause in the contract that gave future kings of Norway the right to redeem the islands for a fixed sum of 210&#160;kg of gold or 2,310&#160;kg of silver. Several attempts were made during the 17th and 18th centuries to redeem the islands, without success.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-109"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-109">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">For example at the Fall of Warness the tide can run at 4&#160;m/s (7.8 knots).<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-144"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-144">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"> Coull (2003) quotes the old saying that an Orcadian is a farmer with a boat, in contrast to a Shetlander, who is a fisherman with a <a href="/wiki/Croft_(land)" title="Croft (land)">croft</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Coull_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Coull-89">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-150"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-150">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"\n\nThe centre offers developers the opportunity to test prototype devices in unrivalled wave and tidal conditions. Wave and tidal energy converters are connected to the national grid via seabed cables running from open-water test berths into an onshore substation. Testing takes place in a wide range of sea and weather conditions, with comprehensive round-the-clock monitoring."<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-167"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-167">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">There is convincing place-name evidence for the Picts\' use of Brythonic or <a href="/wiki/P-Celtic_and_Q-Celtic" class="mw-redirect" title="P-Celtic and Q-Celtic">P-Celtic</a>, although no written records survive. No certain knowledge of any pre-Pictish language exists anywhere in Scotland, but there may well have been times of significant overlap.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> For example, the early Scottish Earls spoke Gaelic when the majority of their subjects spoke Norn, and both of these languages were then replaced by Insular Scots. It is therefore possible that the Pictish aristocracy spoke one language and the common folk an unknown precursor such as <a href="/wiki/Proto-Celtic" class="mw-redirect" title="Proto-Celtic">Proto-Celtic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-170"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-170">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Only two <a href="/wiki/Goidelic_languages" title="Goidelic languages">Q-Celtic</a> words exist in the language of modern Orcadians \xe2\x80\x93 "iper" from <i>eabhar</i>, meaning a <a href="/wiki/Midden" title="Midden">midden</a> slurry, and "keero" from <i>caora</i> \xe2\x80\x93 used to describe a small sheep in the North Isles.<sup id="cite_ref-Lamb_2003_p._250_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lamb_2003_p._250-169">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-174"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-174">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Lamb (2003) counted 60 words "with correlates in Old Norse only" and 500 Scots expressions in common use in the 1950s.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-177"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-177">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The word is of uncertain origin and has also been attested in the Lothians and Fife in the 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-193"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-193">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The expression "ferry louper" has a literal meaning of "ferry jumper" i.e. one who has jumped off a ferry as distinct from a native.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h3><span
